% mdlDerivatives
44
function sys=mdlDerivatives(t,x,u)
45
%% Sorting inputs
46
par = u(1:4); % Parameters
47
feed = u(5:11); % feed, heat duty and flow rate of removed vapor/liquid
48
preL= u(12:15); % liquid from previous stage
49
preV = u(16:19); % vapor from previous stage
50
51
R = par(1); % J/K mol, gas constant
52
P = par(2); % Pa, stage pressure
53
Vol = par(3); % m3, stage volume
54
tres = par(4); % s, residence time
55
Fj = feed(1); % mol/s, total feed flow
56
z1 = feed(2); % water fraction of feed
57
z2 = feed(3); % ethanol fraction of feed
58
TF = feed(4); % K, temperature of feed
59
U = feed(5); % liquid removed
60
W = feed(6); % vapor removed
61
Q = feed(7); % J/s, heat duty, (-) if energy added, (+) if energy removed
62
Ljm1 = preL(1); % mol/s, liquid from stage j-1
63
Tjm1 = preL(2); % K, temperature of previous liquid stage
64
xjm11 = preL(3); % water fraction in previous liquid stage
65
xjm12 = preL(4); % ethanol fraction in previous liquid stage
66
Vjp1 = preV(1); % mol/s, vapor flow rate from previous stage
67
Tjp1 = preV(2); % K, temperature of vapor from previous stage
68
yjp11 = preV(3); % water fraction in vapor from previous stage
69
yjp12 = preV(4); % ethanol fraction in vapor from previous stage
70
%% Properties
71
% Concentrations
72
c_TV = P/(R*x(3)); %mol/m3, ideal gas
73
c_TL = 10*c_TV; %mol/m3, assume equimolar amounts of liquid and vapor
74
75
% Enthalpies
76
% Feed
77
CpwL = 75; %J/mol K, heat capacity, liquid water
78
CpwV = 27; %J/K mol, heat capacity, vapor water
79
CpeL = 112.4; %J/mol K, heat capacity, liquid ethanol
80
CpeV = 87.53; %J/mol K, heat capacity, vapor ethanol
81
H_wLF = 40660 + CpwL*(TF-373.15); %J/mol, enthalpy of water liquid feed
82
H_eLF = 38600 + CpeL*(TF-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol liquid feed
83
H_wVF = 40660 + CpwV*(TF-373.15); %J/mol enthalpy of water vapor feed
84
H_eVF = 38600 + CpeV*(TF-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol vapor feed
85
if Fj == 0 % If statement to avoid division by zero.
86
H_LF = 0;
87
else
88
H_LF = H_wLF*z1+ H_eLF*z2; %J/mol, total liquid feed enthalpy
89
end
90
if Fj == 0 % If statement to avoid division by 0.
91
H_VF = 0;
92
else
93
H_VF = H_wVF*z1 + H_eVF*z2; %J/mol, total vapor feed enthalpy
94
end
95
HF = H_LF + H_VF; % J/mol
96
97
% Previous stages
98
H_Ljm11 =
40660 + CpwL*(Tjm1-373.15); %J/mol, enthalpy of water liquid from previous stage
99
H_Ljm12 = 38600 + CpeL*(Tjm1-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol liquid from prevoius stage
100
H_Vjp11 = 40660 + CpwV*(Tjp1-373.15); %J/mol enthalpy of water vapor from prevoius stage
101
H_Vjp12 = 38600 + CpeV*(Tjp1-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol vapor from prevoius stage
102
Hjm1 = H_Ljm11*xjm11 + H_Ljm12*xjm12; %J/mol enthalpy of liquid from previous stage
103
Hjp1 = H_Vjp11*yjp11 + H_Vjp12*yjp12; %J/mol enthalpy of vapor from previous stage
104
105
% Current stage
106
H_L = x(4) * (40660 + CpwL*(x(3)-373.15)) + x(5) * (38600 + CpeL*(x(3)-352)); %J/mol, liquid enthalpy
107
H_V = x(6) * (40660 + CpwV*(x(3)-373.15)) + x(7) * (38600 + CpeV*(x(3)-352)); %J/mol, vapor enthalpy
108
109
% Equilibrium ratio
110
% Wilson
111
% Lambda matrix
112
Lambda(1,1) = 1;
113
Lambda(2,2) = 1;
114
Lambda(1,2) = exp(-0.0503 - 69.6372./x(3)); % From Aspen documentation
115
Lambda(2,1) = exp(-2.5035 + 346.151./x(3)); % From Aspen documentation
116
% S
117
S1 =
x(4)+x(5)*Lambda(1,2);
118
S2 =
x(5)+x(4)*Lambda(2,1);
119
% Q
120
% First composition derivatives
121
Q1 =
-log(S1) - x(4)/S1 - x(5) * Lambda(2,1)/S2;
122
Q2 =
-log(S2) - x(5)/S2 - x(4) * Lambda(1,2)/S1;
123
% Second composition derivatives
124
Q11 =
-2/S1 + x(4)/S1^2 + x(5)*Lambda(2,1)^2/S2^2;
125
Q12 =
-Lambda(1,2)/S1 - Lambda(2,1)/S2 + x(4)*Lambda(1,2)/S1^2 + x(5)*Lambda(2,1)/S2^2;
126
Q21 =
Q12;
127
Q22 =
-2/S2 + x(5)/S2^2 + x(4)*Lambda(1,2)^2/S1^2;
128
% Activity coefficients
129
lngamma1 =
x(4)+x(5)+Q1;
XXIII
==PAGE:132==
A.3. Matlab scripts and s-functions
June, 2018
130
lngamma2 =
x(4)+x(5)+Q2;
131
gammaWilson1 =
exp(lngamma1);
132
gammaWilson2 =
exp(lngamma2);
133
134
% Vapor pressure
135
Psatw = exp(73.649 - 7258./(x(3))-7.3037.*log(x(3)) + 4.1653e-6 .* x(3).^2); % Pa, from Aspen, extended Antoine
136
Psate = exp(73.304 - 7122.3./(x(3)) -7.1424.*log(x(3)) + 2.8853e-6 .*x(3).^2); %Pa, from Aspen
137
Lambda(1,1) = 1;
138
Lambda(2,2) = 1;
139
140
% K-values
141
Keq1 = Psatw*gammaWilson1/P; % K-value, water
142
Keq2 = Psate*gammaWilson2/P; % K-value, ethanol
143
%% Differential equations
144
% x = [Lj Vj Tj x1 x2 y1 y2 Hj
M1j M2j];
145
% x = [x1 x2 x3 x4 x5 x6 x7 x8
x9
x10];
146
147
MT = Vol*(c_TL+c_TV); % total holdup
148
149
dxdt(8,1) = Ljm1*Hjm1 + Vjp1*Hjp1 + Fj*HF - (x(1)+U)*H_L - (x(2)+W)*H_V - Q; % dHjdt
150
dxdt(9,1) = Ljm1*xjm11 + Vjp1*yjp11 + Fj*z1 - (x(1)+U)*x(4) - (x(2)+W)*x(6); % dM1jdt
151
dxdt(10,1) = Ljm1*xjm12 + Vjp1*yjp12 + Fj*z2 - (x(1)+U)*x(5) - (x(2)+W)*x(7); % dM2jdt
152
153
% dMTdt = dM1dt + dM2dt
154
dxdt(1,1) = 1/tres *0.5* (dxdt(9,1)+dxdt(10,1)); % dLjdt
155
dxdt(2,1) = 1/tres *0.5* (dxdt(9,1)+dxdt(10,1)); % dVjdt
156
157
dxdt(3,1) = 1/(MT*((x(4)*CpwL+x(5)*CpeL)+(x(6)*CpwV+x(7)*CpeV))) * dxdt(8,1); % dTdt
158
159
dxdt(4,1) = 1/((1+1*Keq1)*MT) * dxdt(9,1); % dx1jdt
160
dxdt(5,1) = 1/((1+1*Keq2)*MT) * dxdt(10,1); % dx2jdt
161
dxdt(6,1) = 1/((1/Keq1+1)*MT) * dxdt(9,1); %dy1jdt
162
dxdt(7,1) = 1/((1/Keq2+1)*MT) * dxdt(10,1); %dy2jdt
163
164
sys = [dxdt(1,1) dxdt(2,1) dxdt(3,1) dxdt(4,1) dxdt(5,1) dxdt(6,1) dxdt(7,1) dxdt(8,1) dxdt(9,1) dxdt(10,1)];
165

% mdlOutputs
167
function sys=mdlOutputs(t,x,u)
168
sys = x;

function F = transfer_test(par,x,constvars)
2
%% Constant variables:
3
%constvars = Lj Vj TL TV x1 x2 y1 y2
4
% Bulk values are constant
5
Lj = constvars(1);
6
Vj = constvars(2);
7

8
TV = constvars(4);
9
x1 = constvars(5);

x2 = constvars(6);
11
y1 = constvars(7);
12
y2 = constvars(8);
13
%% Known parameters
14
%par = [R N P L0 D u_v u_l Phi_L h l_0 aI aC aC_V aC_L]
15
R = par(1); %J/K mol, gas constant not used
16
N = par(2); %number of stages
17

% Dimensions

u_l = par(7); %mF/s, linear liquid velocity
24
% Filling fraction

%% Properties

c_TV = (Vj)/(aC_V*u_v); %mol/m3
36
c_TL = (Lj)/(aC_L*u_l); %mol/m3,
37
38
% Enthalpies
39
% Phase
40
H_wL =
40660 + 75*(TL-373.15); %J/mol, enthalpy of water liquid
41
H_eL =
38600 + 112.4*(TL-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol liquid
42
H_wV =
40660 + 27*(TV-373.15); %J/mol enthalpy of water vapor feed,
43
H_eV =
38600 + 87.53*(TV-352); %J/mol, enthalpy of ethanol vapor
44
45
H_L =
H_wL*x1 + H_eL*x2; %J/mol, total liquid enthalpy
46
H_Lpar1 =
H_wL; %J/mol, enthalpy of liquid water
47
H_Lpar2 =
H_eL; %J/mol, enthalpy of liquid ethanol
48
H_V =
H_wV*y1 + H_eV*y2; %J/mol, total vapor enthalpy
49
H_Vpar1 =
H_wV; %J/mol, enthalpy of vapor water
50
H_Vpar2 =
H_eV; %J/mol, enthalpy of vapor ethanol
51
52
% Transfer cofficients
53
Tprop =x(1)-273.15; %C, correlations are for T in celsius
54
% Properties,
55
% Assume liquid is water and vapor phase is ethanol/air
56
% Densities
57
rho_wl =
exp(6.9094-2.0146*10^(-5)*Tprop-5.9868*10^(-6)*Tprop^2 + 2.5921 * 10^(-8) * Tprop^3 - ...
9.3244*10^(-11)*Tprop^4+1.2103*10^(-13)*Tprop^5); %kg/m3, density of liquid water
58
rho_wv =
exp(-5.3225+6.8366*10^(-2)*Tprop-2.7243*10^(-4)*Tprop^2 + 8.4522 * 10^(-7) * Tprop^3 - ...
1.65581*10^(-9)*Tprop^4+1.5514*10^(-12)*Tprop^5); %kg/m3, density of water vapor
59
60
mu_wl =
exp(9.7620-3.1154*10^(-2)*Tprop+2.0029*10^(-4)*Tprop^2 - 9.5815 * 10^(-7) * Tprop^3 + ...
2.7772*10^(-9)*Tprop^4-3.5075*10^(-12)*Tprop^5)*10^(-7); %N s/m, viscosity of water liquid
61
mu_wv =
exp(4.3995+3.8789*10^(-3)*Tprop+2.1181*10^(-5)*Tprop^2 - 3.4406 * 10^(-7) * Tprop^3 + ...
1.6730*10^(-9)*Tprop^4-2.8030*10^(-12)*Tprop^5)*10^(-7); %N s/m, viscosity of water vapor
62
63
lambda_wl =
exp(-5.6528*10^(-1)+3.1743*10^(-3)*Tprop-1.4392 * 10^(-5) * Tprop^2 - 1.3224 * ...
10^(-8)*Tprop^3+2.5534*10^(-10)*Tprop^4-6.4454*10^(-13)*Tprop^5); %J/m s K, thermal conductivity of liquid water
64
lambda_wv =
exp(-4.0406+3.228*10^(-3)*Tprop+5.3383*10^(-6)*Tprop^2 - 6.7139 * 10^(-8) * ...
Tprop^3+4.0967*10^(-10)*Tprop^4-6.9579*10^(-13)*Tprop^5); %J/m s K, thermal conductivity of water vapor
65
66
Cp_wl =
exp(1.4338-2.2638*10^(-4)*Tprop+4.2819*10^(-6)*Tprop^2 - 2.7411 * 10^(-8) * Tprop^3 + ...
1.4699*10^(-10)*Tprop^4-2.2589*10^(-13)*Tprop^5)*10^3; %J/kg K, specific heat capacity of liquid water
67
Cp_wv =
exp(6.2084*10^(-1)+3.1420*10^(-4)*Tprop+1.6110*10^(-6) * Tprop^2 + 4.0156 * ...
10^(-8)*Tprop^3+3.4841*10^(-11)*Tprop^4-2.0709*10^(-13)*Tprop^5)*10^3; %J/kg K, specific heat capacity of water vapor
68
69
D_wel = 0.69*10^(-9); %m/2, diffusion coefficient of water in ethanol liquid. Article Hills et al
70
D_wav = 24*10^(-6); %m2/s, diffusion coefficient of water in air (ethanol) Mass Diffusivity Data by Isidoro Martinez
71
72
% Dimensionless numbers
73
Re_wv =
rho_wv*u_v*l_0/mu_wv; %Reynolds number for vapor water phase
74
Re_wl =
rho_wl*u_l*l_0/mu_wl; %Reynolds number for liquid water phase
75
Sc_wv =
mu_wv/(rho_wv*D_wav); %Schmidt number for vapor water phase, water in air
76
Sc_wl =
mu_wl/(rho_wl*D_wel); %Schmidt number for liquid water phase, water in water
77
Pr_wv =
Cp_wv*mu_wv/lambda_wv; %Prandtl number for vapor phase water
78
Pr_wl =
Cp_wl*mu_wl/lambda_wl; %Prandtl number for liquid phase water
79
80
% From Transport Phenomena: Flat plate geometry
81
jD_wv =
0.332*Re_wv^(-1/2); %Chilton-Colburn j-factor for diffusion, water vapor
82
jD_wl =
0.332*Re_wl^(-1/2); %Chilton-Colburn j-factor for diffusion, water liquid
83
jH_wv =
jD_wv; %Chilton-Colburn j-factor for heat, water vapor
84
jH_wl =
jD_wl; %Chilton-Colburn j-factor for heat, water liquid
85
86
% Mass and heat transfer coefficient
87
% jD = Sh/(Re Sc^(1/3)), jH = Nu/(Re Pr^(1/3))
88
% Nu = h*l0/lambda, Sh = k*l0/D_AB
89
% flat plane
90
k_wev =
jD_wv*Re_wv*Sc_wv^(1/3)*D_wav*1/l_0; %m/s, mass transfer coefficient for water in ethanol(air) in vapor phase
91
k_wel =
jD_wl*Re_wl*Sc_wl^(1/3)*D_wel*1/l_0; %m/s, mass transfer coefficient for water in ethanol liquid phase
92
93
% Assigning the mass transfer coefficients in a matrix
94
k_v(1,1) =
0;
95
k_v(1,2) =
k_wev;
96
k_v(2,1) =
k_v(1,2);
97
k_v(2,2) =
0;
98
k_l(1,1) =
0;
99
k_l(1,2) =
k_wel;
100
k_l(2,1) =
k_l(1,2);
101
k_l(2,2) =
0;
102
% Flat plane
103
h_wv =
jH_wv*Re_wv*Pr_wv^(1/3)*lambda_wv*1/l_0; %J/m2 s K, heat transfer coefficient for water in vapor phase
104
h_wl =
jH_wl*Re_wl*Pr_wl^(1/3)*lambda_wl*1/l_0; %J/m2 s K, heat transfer coefficient for water in liquid phase
105
106
h_v =
h_wv; % W/m2 K, total heat transfer coefficient in vapor phase
107
h_l =
h_wl; % W/m2 K, total heat transfer coefficient in liquid phase
108
109
% Activity coefficient for binary system
110
% Molar volumes
111
V1 = 0.0188311/1000; %m3/mol, water molar volume
112
V2 = 0.0626953/1000; %m3/mol, ethanol molar volume
113
% A matrix
114
A11 = 0;
115
A22 = 0;
116
A12 = -472.30+4.4808*x(1) - 0.005102*x(1)^2; %K, A12/R
117
A21 = -2007.08+10.8519*x(1)-0.013084*x(1)^2; %K, A21/R
XXVII
==PAGE:136==
A.3. Matlab scripts and s-functions
June, 2018
118
% Lambda matrix
119
Lambda(1,1) = V1/V1 * exp(-A11/(R*x(1)));
120
Lambda(2,2) = V2/V2 * exp(-A22/(R*x(1)));
121
Lambda(1,2) = V2/V1 * exp(-A12/(x(1)));
122
Lambda(2,1) = V1/V2 * exp(-A21/(x(1)));
123
% S
124
S1 =
x(4)+x(5)*Lambda(1,2);
125
S2 =
x(5)+x(4)*Lambda(2,1);
126
% Q
127
% First composition derivatives
128
Q1 =
-log(S1) - x(4)/S1 - x(5) * Lambda(2,1)/S2;
129
Q2 =
-log(S2) - x(5)/S2 - x(4) * Lambda(1,2)/S1;
130
% Second composition derivatives
131
Q11 =
-2/S1 + x(4)/S1^2 + x(5)*Lambda(2,1)^2/S2^2;
132
Q12 =
-Lambda(1,2)/S1 - Lambda(2,1)/S2 + x(4)*Lambda(1,2)/S1^2 + x(5)*Lambda(2,1)/S2^2;
133
Q21 =
Q12;
134
Q22 =
-2/S2 + x(5)/S2^2 + x(4)*Lambda(1,2)^2/S1^2;
135
% Activity coefficients
136
lngamma1 =
x(4)+x(5)+Q1;
137
lngamma2 =
x(4)+x(5)+Q2;
138
gammaWilson1 =
exp(lngamma1);
139
gammaWilson2 =
exp(lngamma2);
140
% Thermodynamic factor
141
Gamma(1,1) =
Q11 - x(4)*Q11 - x(5)*Q21;
142
Gamma(1,2) =
Q12 - x(4)*Q12 - x(5)*Q22;
143
Gamma(2,1) =
Q21 - x(5)*Q21 - x(4)*Q11;
144
Gamma(2,2) =
Q22 - x(5)*Q22 - x(4)*Q12;
145
146
% Vapor pressure from Antoine
147
% For water, the Antoine parameters are
148
% From NIST
149
if TL ≥380 % High temperature Antoine coefficients
150
Aw = 3.55959;
151
Bw = 643.748;
152
Cw = -198.043;
153
Ae = 4.9531;
154
Be = 1432.526;
155
Ce = -61.819;
156
elseif TL < 380 % Low temperature Antoine coefficients
157
Aw = 5.20389;
158
Bw = 1733.926;
159
Cw = -39.485;
160
Ae = 5.24677;
161
Be = 1598.673;
162
Ce = -46.424;
163
end
164
Psatw =
10^(Aw-Bw/(x(1)+Cw))*10^5; %Pa, vapor pressure for water
165
Psate =
10^(Ae-Be/(x(1)+Ce))*10^5; %Pa, vapor pressure for ethanol
166
% Equilibrium ratio
167
Keq1 =
Psatw*gammaWilson1/P;
168
Keq2 =
Psate*gammaWilson2/P;
169
170
% Transfer rates, 2 component system only kappa(1,1) is necessary. Sum of flux = 0
171
RV(1,1) =
x(6)/k_v(1,2) + x(7)/k_v(1,2); % inverse vapor transfer coefficient
172
RL(1,1) =
x(4)/k_l(1,2) + x(5)/k_l(1,2); % inverse liquid transfer coefficient
173
174
kappa_V(1,1) =
RV(1,1)^(-1); % corrected vapor transfer coefficient
175
kappa_L(1,1) =
RL(1,1)^(-1)*Gamma(1,1); % corrected liquid transfer coefficient
176
177
J_V1 =
c_TV*kappa_V(1,1)*(y1-x(6)); %mol/s m2, water flux in vapor phase
178
J_V2 =
-J_V1; %mol/s m2, ethanol flux in vapor phase
179
J_L1 =
c_TL*kappa_L(1,1)*(x(4)-x1); %mol/s m2, water flux in liquid phase
180
J_L2 =
-J_L1; %mol/s m2, ethanol flux in liquid phase
181
182
N_T =
x(2)+x(3); %mol/s, total material transfer rate
183
N_V1 =
aI*J_V1 + y1*N_T;
%mol/s, transfer rate of water vapor
184
N_V2 =
aI*J_V2 + y2*N_T; %mol/s, transfer rate of ethanol vapor
185
N_L1 =
aI*J_L1 + x1*N_T; %mol/s, transfer rate of water liquid
186
N_L2 =
aI*J_L2 + x2*N_T; %mol/s, transfer rate of ethanol liquid
187
188
e_L =
aI*h_l*(x(1)-TL) +
(N_L1*H_Lpar1+N_L2*H_Lpar2); %J/s, heat transfer rate, liquid
189
e_V =
aI*h_v*(TV-x(1)) +
(N_V1*H_Vpar1+N_V2*H_Vpar2); %J/s, heat transfer rate, vapor
190
191
%% Eqns.
192
% x = TI, N1, N2, x1I, x2I, y1I, y2I, interface variables
193
% x = x1, x2, x3, x4,
x5,
x6,
x7
194
F(1) = N_L1 - x(2);
%RL
195
F(2) = N_V1 - x(2);
%RV
196
F(3) = e_L - e_V;
%EI
197
F(4) = Keq1 * x(4) - x(6);
%Q1
198
F(5) = Keq2*x(5) - x(7);
%Q2
199
F(6) = x(6) + x(7) - 1;
%S1
200
F(7) = x(4) + x(5) -1;
%S2

function F=aspen_test(constvars_aspen,x)
2
%% Example from Taylor, Aspen values
3
% constvars_aspen = [k_l k_v TL TV x1 x2 y1 y2 c_L c_V P R h_L h_V]
4
% x = [TI N1 N2 x1I x2I y1I y2I]
5
% Constant variables from aspen
6
k_l = constvars_aspen(1);
7
k_v = constvars_aspen(2);
8
TL = constvars_aspen(3);
9
TV = constvars_aspen(4);
10
x1 = constvars_aspen(5);
11
x2 = constvars_aspen(6);
12
y1 = constvars_aspen(7);
13
y2 = constvars_aspen(8);
14
c_L = constvars_aspen(9);
15
c_V = constvars_aspen(10);
16
P = constvars_aspen(11);
17
R = constvars_aspen(12);
18
h_L = constvars_aspen(13);
19
h_V = constvars_aspen(14);
20
% enthalpies
21
H_w = 5.66e+7 * (1-x(1)/647.1)^(0.61204-0.6257*x(1)/647.1 +0.3988*(x(1)/647.1)^2)/10^3; %J/mol, Aspen correlation
22
H_e = 6.5831e+7*(1-x(1)/514)^(1.1905-1.7666*x(1)/514 + 1.0012*(x(1)/514)^2)/10^3; %J/mol, Aspen correlation
23
% Vapor pressure
24
Psatw = exp(73.649-7258./(x(1)+0)+0*x(1)-7.3037*log(x(1))+4.1653e-6 * x(1)^2); % Pa, from Aspen, extended Antoine
25
Psate = exp(73.304 - 7122.3/(x(1)+0) +0*x(1) -7.1424*log(x(1)) +2.8853e-6*x(1)^2); %Pa, from Aspen
26
% Heat capaicities
27
Cp_wV = (33363+26790*((2610.5/x(1))/sinh(2610.5/x(1)))^2 + 8896*((1169/x(1))/cosh(1169/x(1)))^2)/10^3; % J/mol K, water vapor ...
heat capacity from aspen
28
Cp_eV = (49200 + 145770*((1662.8/x(1))/sinh(1662.8/x(1)))^2+93900*((744.7/x(1))/cosh(744.7/x(1)))^2)/10^3; % J/mol K, ethanol ...
vapor heat capacity from aspen
29
% Activity coefficients
30
% Lambda matrix
31
Lambda(1,1) = 1;
32
Lambda(2,2) = 1;
33
Lambda(1,2) = exp(-0.0503 - 69.6372/x(1)); % From Aspen documentation
34
Lambda(2,1) = exp(-2.5035 + 346.151/x(1)); % From Aspen documentation
35
% lngamma
36
lngamma1 =
1 - log(x(4)*Lambda(1,1)+x(5)*Lambda(1,2)) - (Lambda(1,1)*x(4)/(Lambda(1,1)*x(4) + Lambda(1,2)*x(5)) + ...
Lambda(2,1)*x(5)/(Lambda(2,1)*x(4)+Lambda(2,2)*x(5)));
37
lngamma2 =
1 - log(x(4)*Lambda(2,1)+x(5)*Lambda(2,2)) - (Lambda(1,2)*x(4)/(Lambda(1,1)*x(4) + Lambda(1,2)*x(5)) + ...
Lambda(2,2)*x(5)/(Lambda(2,1)*x(4)+Lambda(2,2)*x(5)));
38
39
gammaWilson1 =
exp(lngamma1);
40
gammaWilson2 =
exp(lngamma2);
41
42
%% Equations
43
PHI_V = (x(2)+x(3))/(c_V*k_v);
44
CORFAC_V = PHI_V/(exp(PHI_V)-1); % Vapor correction
45
46
PHI_L = (x(2)+x(3))/(c_L*k_l);
47
CORFAC_L = PHI_L * exp(PHI_L)/(exp(PHI_L)-1); % Liquid correction
48
49
PHI_H_V = (x(2)*Cp_wV + x(3)*Cp_eV)/h_V;
50
CORFAC_H_V = PHI_H_V/(exp(PHI_H_V)-1); % Vapor heat correction
51
52
JV1 = c_V * k_v * CORFAC_V * (y1-x(6)); % J/m2 s, water flux in vapor
53
JL1 = c_L * k_l * CORFAC_L * (x(4)-x1); % J/m2 s, ethanol flux in liquid
54
55
F(1) = JV1 + y1 * (x(2)+x(3)) - x(2); % Vapor water balance
56
F(2) =
- h_L*(x(1)-TL) + h_V *CORFAC_H_V*(TV-x(1)) + (x(2) * H_w + x(3) * H_e); % Energy balance
57
F(3) = JL1 + x1*(x(2)+x(3)) - x(2); % Liquid water balance
58
F(4) = Psatw*gammaWilson1*x(4)/P - x(6); % Water equilibrium
59
F(5) = Psate*gammaWilson2/P * x(5) - x(7); % ethanol equilibrium
60
F(6) = x(6) + x(7) -1; % Summation of y
61
F(7) = x(4) + x(5) -1; % Summation of x

y(4)+y(5)*Lambda(1,2);

y(5)+y(4)*Lambda(2,1);

-log(S1) - y(4)/S1 - y(5) * Lambda(2,1)/S2;

Aw = 5.20389;

Cw = -39.485;

10^(Ae-Be/(y(3)+Ce))*10^5; %Pa, vapor pressure for ethanol

F(1) = y(2) - Fj*beta;
110
F(2) = y(4) - z1/(1+beta*(Keq1-1));
111
F(3) = y(5) - z2/(1+beta*(Keq2-1));
112
F(4) = y(6) - y(4)*Keq1;
113
F(5) = y(7) - y(5)*Keq2;
114
F(6) = Fj - y(1) - y(2);
115
F(7) = (beta*H_V + (1-beta) * H_L - HF);
116
117
sys = F;
Packed column correlations.
packedcolumncorrelations.m
1
Le_wv = Sc_wv/Pr_wv; % Lewis number for vapor phase water
2
Le_wl = Sc_wl/Pr_wl; % Lewis number for liquid phase water
3
4
% From Multi component mass transfer. Randomly packed column, Bravo & Fair.
5
k_wev = 50*D_wel*2*Re_wv^(0.7)*Sc_wv^(0.333)*(50*l_0)^(-2); % m/s, ap = 50 m2/m3, dp = 0.005 m, A = 2 for dp<0.012. dp = l_0
6
k_wel = 0.0051*Re_wl^(0.667)*Sc_wl^(-0.5)*(50*l_0)^(0.4) * 1 / (rho_wl / (mu_wl*9.81))^0.333; %m/s
7
8
% Randomly packed column, Chilton-Colburn, sep book
9
h_wv = k_wev*rho_wv*Cp_wv*Le_wv^(2/3); % J/m2 s K
10
h_wl = k_wel*rho_wl*Cp_wl*Le_wl^(1/2); % J/m2 s K
Example of how the models are called and plots are produced. Example is for the opti-
mized diabatic tank model.
opt_HI_MC_call.m

%% Parameters
6
%%%% Stripping
7
%Known parameters
8
R = 8.314; %J/K mol, gas constant not used
9
N = 30; %number of stages
10
P =0.1*10^5; %Pa, stage pressure
11
% Dimensions of vessel
12
L0 = 6; %m, length of tank
13
D = 1.8; %m, diameter of tanks
14
aC = pi*(D/2)^2; %m2, total cross-sectional area
15
% Linear velocities
16
u_v = 1e-2; %m/s, vapor velocity
17
u_l = 1e-2; %m/s, liquid velocity
18
h = D/2; %m, height of liquid
19
aC_V = pi*(D/2)^2 - (D/2)^2*acos((D/2-h)/(D/2)) + (D/2-h) * sqrt(2*D/2*h-h^2);% m2, vapor cross-sectional area
20
aC_L = aC - aC_V; % m2, liquid cross-sectional area
21
% filling fraction
22
Phi_L = aC_L/aC; % volume fraction of liquid
23
l_0 = 0.001; %m, characterstic length.
24
aI = 25.450; %m2 , interfacial area
25
par_strip = [R N P L0 D u_v u_l Phi_L h l_0 aI aC aC_V aC_L];
26
%%%% Rectifying
27
%Known parameters
28
R = 8.314; %J/K mol, gas constant not used
29
N = 30; %number of stages
30
P =0.3*10^5; %Pa, stage pressure
31
% Dimensions of vessel
32
L0 = 6; %m, length of tank
33
Di = 1.8; %m, diameter of inner tank
34
D = Di + 0.2; %m, diameter of tank. An additional 10 cm in radius for outer tank
35
Rfilm = Di/2 + 0.005; %m, distance from center to film surface on inner tank, assuming 5mm film thickness
36
aC = pi*(D/2)^2-pi*(Di/2)^2; %m2, cross sectional area of tank minus the inner tank
37
% Linear velocities
38
u_v = 1e-2; %m/s, vapor velocity
39
u_l = 1e-2; %m/s, liquid velocity
40
h = 0.05; %m, height of liquid in outer shell, assume 5 cm of liquid in bottom of outer shell
41
aC_V = pi*(D/2)^2 - (D/2)^2*acos((D/2-h)/(D/2)) + (D/2-h) * sqrt(2*D/2*h-h^2) - pi*Rfilm^2;% m2, vapor cross-sectional area
42
aC_L = aC - aC_V; % m2, liquid cross-sectional area
43
% filling fraction
44
Phi_L = aC_L/aC; % volume fraction of liquid
45
l_0 = 0.001; %m, characterstic length.
46
aI = 4*25.450; %m2 , interfacial area
47
par_rect = [R N P L0 D u_v u_l Phi_L h l_0 aI aC aC_V aC_L]; % parameters input
